Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
beginner
8 min
Definition of Istihsan by Imam al-Karkhi
Introduces subsidiary sources and provides a precise definition of istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam al-Karkhi's definition of istihsan and identify the wajh aqwa (stronger reason) as the key condition distinguishing it from arbitrary preference.

Core Idea
Istihsan: turning from qiyas to another ruling due to a stronger legal reason.

Istihsan is a subsidiary source in Hanafi methodology that allows a jurist to set aside the apparent analogy in favor of a different ruling when a stronger evidence demands it. Imam al-Karkhi's definition captures this precisely. This lesson unpacks his definition and clarifies that istihsan is not arbitrary but grounded in valid legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three subsidiary sources mentioned
The passage lists istihsan, istislah (masalih mursala), and urf as the main subsidiary sources.
2
Understand their derivative nature
These sources are subsidiary to and reducible to the four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas).
3
Memorize al-Karkhi's definition
Istihsan is 'turning away from the ruling of a case to a different ruling from its analogues due to a stronger reason that necessitates this deviation.'
4
Break down the definition into key elements
The definition has five components: (1) al-udul (turning away), (2) an hukm nadha'iriha (from ruling of its analogues), (3) ila hukm akhar (to another ruling), (4) li wajh aqwa (for a stronger reason), (5) yaqtadi hadha al-udul (that necessitates this turning).
5
Appreciate why this definition is preferred
Al-Karkhi's definition is comprehensive because it covers all types of istihsan (by nass, ijma, darura, urf, and qiyas khafi).

Source Text

الفصل الرابع
المصادر التبعية : الاستحسان

AV
Chapter Four: Subsidiary Sources: Istihsan. 1/4 – There are other legitimate bases for proving fiqh rulings besides the four primary sources mentioned above, and the texts of the Book and the Sunnah indicate that they are considered valid bases for proving rulings. However, these sources are in fact subsidiary, branching from the four primary sources. Therefore, most scholars do not count them as additional but consider them reducible to those primary sources. And the most important of those subsidiary sources are three, which we will explain in this chapter and the two following chapters: (1) Istihsan, (2) al-Istislah or the principle of masalih mursala (public interest), and (3) al-'Urf (custom). Section One: Istihsan. 2/4 – Istihsan is: turning away from the ruling of a case to a different ruling from its analogues due to a stronger reason that necessitates this deviation. This is what Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, one of the imams of the Hanafi school, defines it with. And it is perhaps the best of the transmitted definitions of istihsan and the most comprehensive for its types to be explained later. (Ref: Kashf al-Asrar Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi, 3/4, and the book 'Abu Hanifa' by Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra, part two, p. 174.)
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from al-Zarqa's introduction introduces the subsidiary sources of Islamic law, focusing on istihsan (juristic preference). First, it explains that there are other legitimate bases besides the four primary sources (Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, Qiyas), but these are ultimately derivative of the four. The three main subsidiary sources are: istihsan, istislah (consideration of public interest), and urf (custom). The passage then provides the definition of istihsan by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), a leading Hanafi jurist. According to him, istihsan is the departure from the ruling that would normally apply to a case by analogy (qiyas) to a different ruling, due to a stronger reason (wajh aqwa) that justifies this departure. This definition is preferred because it covers all types of istihsan, including istihsan by text (nass), consensus (ijma), necessity (darura), custom (urf), and hidden analogy (qiyas khafi). For the Hanafi student, istihsan is a key methodological tool that allows flexibility and prevents rigidity in applying qiyas. It is often used in areas like commercial transactions and family law to achieve equity and practicality.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Turning away from the ruling of a case to a different ruling from its analogues due to a stronger reason that necessitates this deviation.
المصادر التبعية (al-masadir al-tabi'a): Subsidiary legal sources that derive from and are reducible to the four primary sources.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Karkhi's definition, what is istihsan?
A) Following the apparent analogy in all cases.
B) Departing from the ruling of analogues to another ruling due to a stronger reason.
C) Rejecting all analogies.
D) Following personal opinion without evidence.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Karkhi's definition establishes istihsan as a disciplined departure from qiyas based on a stronger legal evidence, not personal preference.

Rule of Predominance: Benefit and Harm Weighed by the Preponderant Aspect
Stating the qawida that the preponderant aspect determines whether something is maslahah or mafsadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'al-ghalib' to determine the ruling of an action with mixed benefit and harm, and identify when the subordinate aspect is disregarded.

Core Idea
The Shari'ah judges by the predominant benefit or harm, not by incidental aspects.

This lesson introduces a foundational legal maxim of Hanafi usul: when any action or matter has both beneficial and harmful aspects, the Shari'ah gives weight to the preponderant side. This principle underlies many rulings in fiqh, from the permissibility of medical treatment despite side effects to the prohibition of usury despite some apparent benefit. Understanding this qawida is essential for a mufti to correctly apply the Maqasid al-Shari'ah.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its key terms
Identify the Arabic text of the qawida: 'كل أمر فيه جهتا نفع وضرر؛ والعبرة شرعاً للغالب'. Define 'al-ghalib' (predominant) and 'al-marjuh' (subordinate).
The maxim applies to any matter with mixed aspects.
2
Identify the scope of the maxim
Recognize that this qawida governs all chapters of fiqh where an action has both benefit and harm, particularly in determining rulings for commanded and prohibited acts.
3
Apply the maxim to the furuat examples
Work through the two examples given: commanded actions (matalubat) where subordinate harm is disregarded, and prohibited actions (makruhat) where subordinate benefit is disregarded.
In matalubat, the harm is like thorns on the path; in makruhat, the benefit is like profit from a disgraceful act.
4
Identify the istithna' (exception)
Note that when benefit and harm are exactly equal, the maxim does not apply. The default rule of 'al-asl fi al-ashya' al-ibahah' (original permissibility) governs unless further evidence is found.
Equality triggers a different treatment.
5
Relate to complementary qawaid
Connect this maxim with 'al-darar yuzal' (harm must be removed) and 'al-mashaqqah tajlib al-taysir' (hardship begets ease) to see how they work together.
These qawaid complement each other in practical legal reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

هذا،
ومن المسلم به أن كل أمر من الأمور فيه جهة نفع وجهة ضرر متعادلتان أو متفاوتتان فإذا كانت جهة النفع في الشيء هي الغالبة فهو مصلحة بالمعنى العرفي وإن اشتمل على ضرر مغلوب. وإذا كانت جهة الضرر هي الغالبة فهو مفسدة بالمعنى العرفي وإن اشتمل على نفع مغلوب. ولذا كان الفعل ذو الوجهين منسوباً إلى الجهة الراجحة فيه من مصلحة أو مفسدة، أي من نفع أو ضرر.

الشخص في الترك إنما هو اجتناب العمل الشائن، لا اجتناب الربح. ومن المقرر أيضاً أن المصالح التي يعتبرها الشرع ويرعاها لا عبرة لكونها موافقة لأهواء المكلفين وشهواتهم أو مخالفة، وإنما هي ما يقيم شأن الدنيا على أن تكون جسراً للآخرة، فتبني حياة صالحة فاضلة متعاونة على الخير والبر.

Chapter 5: Subsidiary Sources: al-Istislah

5/5 - Every matter has two aspects: benefit and harm; and the legal consideration is given to the predominant aspect:

This is so, and it is accepted that every matter has an aspect of benefit and an aspect of harm, either equal or varying. If the aspect of benefit in something is predominant, then it is a benefit in the customary sense even if it includes a subordinate harm. And if the aspect of harm is predominant, then it is a harm in the customary sense even if it includes a subordinate benefit. Hence, an action with two aspects is attributed to the prevailing aspect of benefit or harm, i.e., of profit or loss.
Accordingly, every thing or action is either permissible or prohibited based on the preponderance of its benefit or the preponderance of its harm, not because it is pure benefit or pure harm. And the assessment of that is left to the consideration of the Lawgiver.
It is also established in this case that the subordinate, overwhelmed aspect of benefit or harm is not intended by the Lawgiver in His commands and prohibitions; rather, it is disregarded for the sake of the predominant aspect.
- In commanded matters, the subordinate harm is like thorns on the road leading to the goal; these thorns are not intended for the traveler.
- In prohibited matters, the subordinate benefit is like material profit in a disgraceful act that a person abhors; that profit is not intended to be avoided for its own sake, but the person's intention in avoiding is to shun the disgraceful act, not to avoid the profit.
It is also established that the benefits that the Shari'ah considers and protects are not measured by whether they conform to the desires and passions of the obligated individuals or oppose them; rather, they are what put the affairs of this world in order to be a bridge to the Hereafter, building a righteous, virtuous life cooperating in goodness and piety.
Imam al-Shatibi clarified this meaning and exhaustively presented evidence for it in al-Muwafaqat (2/26 and 27) and said:
All this consideration is based on the fact that benefits are legislated for the establishment of this worldly life, not for the attainment of desires nor for responding to the call of whims.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage presents a key qawida (legal maxim) of Hanafi usul: when an action has both benefit and harm, the Shari'ah gives weight to the predominant aspect. The author explains that something is considered a maslahah if its benefit predominates over its harm, even if some harm remains; conversely, it is a mafsadah if harm predominates, even if some benefit remains. This principle applies to all rulings: permissibility and prohibition are based on the preponderance of benefit or harm, not on absolute purity. The passage then provides two examples to illustrate how the subordinate aspect is not the focus of the Lawgiver: in commanded actions (matalubat), the subordinate harm is like thorns on a path to a goal—they are not intended; in prohibited actions (makruhat), the subordinate benefit is like profit from a disgraceful act—the prohibition targets the act, not the incidental profit. Finally, the text emphasizes that Shari'ah benefits are not defined by human whims but by the objective of making worldly life a bridge to the Hereafter, citing al-Shatibi's al-Muwafaqat.

Key Terms
الغالب (al-ghalib): The predominant aspect (of benefit or harm) that determines the ruling.
المرجوح (al-marjuh): The subordinate, overwhelmed aspect that is not intended by the Shari'ah in its commands and prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida presented, how is a thing or action judged by the Shari'ah?
A) By its pure benefit regardless of any harm.
B) By the preponderance of its benefit or harm.
C) By the intention of the individual alone.
D) By the majority opinion of scholars.

Key Takeaway
The Shari'ah's consideration is for the predominant aspect of benefit or harm; the subordinate aspect is disregarded.

مبدأ سد الذرائع: Principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i'
Explains the principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i' with Quranic and Prophetic examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i', identify its scriptural evidence, and apply it to contemporary cases by evaluating whether an act should be blocked based on its potential outcome, using the Hanafi fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Sadd al-Dhara'i': an act is prohibited not for itself, but to block the path to evil, even if the actor intends good.

The principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i' (blocking the means) is a fundamental tool in Hanafi legal reasoning, used to prevent permissible acts from leading to prohibited outcomes. This lesson explores its scriptural foundations and juristic applications, highlighting its role in family law and commercial transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle's definition and scope
Understand that Sadd al-Dhara'i' prohibits an act because it typically leads to haram, regardless of intention. The Quranic example of insulting idols illustrates that even good intention does not permit a means that leads to greater harm.
Contrast with principles like 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' which focus on intention.
2
Examine the textual evidence (dalil)
Analyze the Quranic (proposing during 'iddah) and Prophetic (building mosques over graves, bequest to heir, seclusion) examples cited. These are dalil naqli establishing the principle.
All examples are from the passage; note that the Quranic example of insulting idols is also a key proof.
3
Distinguish between intention and outcome
The principle focuses on objective consequences, not subjective intent. The Quran forbids insulting polytheists' idols despite the doer's faith.
This distinguishes Sadd al-Dhara'i' from other principles that consider intention.
4
Apply the principle to juristic rulings
Work through the examples: talaq al-firar (divorce to deprive inheritance) and seller's disclaimer of hidden defects. In talaq al-firar, the wife inherits despite divorce; in sale, a knowing seller cannot disclaim liability.
Note that in both cases, the act itself (divorce, stipulation) is permissible, but becomes prohibited due to the consequence.
5
Evaluate the exceptions (istithna')
The principle does not apply when the means typically does not lead to harm, or when necessity outweighs the risk (e.g., al-darura tubih al-mahzurat).
This prevents over-rigidity and maintains balance with other qawa'id.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
وكذلك حَرَّم القرآن خطبة المرأة المعتدة بعد انقضاء زواجها بطلاق أو بوفاة الزوج حتى تنقضي عدتها كي لا تؤدي خطبتها إلى إخلال بواجب العدة الخطير الذي يقتضيه نظام الأسرة وحقوق الزوجية السابقة. ولذا كان أيضاً عقد الزواج على المرأة المعتدة، ولو بلا دخول غير منعقد شرعاً . ومن شواهد مبدأ سد الذرائع في السنة النبوية أنَّ النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام نهى عن بناء المساجد على القبور وذلك كيلا تفضي إلى عبادة الموتى من عظماء الناس.
وكذلك منع النبي الله الوصية للوارث كي لا تُتَّخذ ذريعة إلى تفضيل بعض الورثة على بعض احتيالاً على نظام الإرث، فإن هذا التفضيل ممنوع شرعاً كما سنرى ف (۸/۲۳(۱) .
وكذلك نهى النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام عن خلوة الرجل بامرأة أجنبية عنه، لأنَّ هذه الخلوة ذريعة يمكن أن تفضي إلى الفساد، ومن الواجب درء المفاسد .
يتضح من هذه الأمثلة الملاحظات التالية :
۱ - أنَّ مبدأ سد الذرائع سلكته الشريعة الإسلامية في الأمور الدينية والمدنية على السواء. فالدينية كمنع بناء المساجد على القبور، والمدنية كالوصية للوارث .
۲ - أنَّ المنظور إليه في سد الذرائع ليس هو النية السيئة من الفاعل، بل مجرد كون الفعل مما يفضي إلى النتيجة التي يأباها الشرع، ولو كان الفاعل حسن النية ولذا نهى القرآن عن سب أصنام المشركين، وإن كان الذي يسبها إنما يسبّها إيماناً بالله تعالى، وانتصاراً له .
والفقهاء المجتهدون بدلالة هذه النصوص وأمثالها المتصلة بحكمة التشريع وسياسته والتي ترشد إلى مبدأ سد الذرائع، قد لجؤوا إلى هذا المبدأ في أحكام اجتهادية قرروها على أساسه :
(1) فمن ذلك ما قرره الاجتهاد في أكثر من مذهب من أنَّ للزوجة المطلقة في طلاق الفرار حق الإرث من زوجها الذي طلقها، لكيلا يتخذ من حقه في الطلاق ذريعة إلى حرمان الزوجة ميراثها المشروع عند يأسه من الحياة بقصد المضارة.
وهذا من قبيل منع التعسف في استعمال الحق، إذ ليس من المصلحة تمكين الناس من هذا التعسف.
- وكذلك قرر الفقهاء أن البائع إذا شرط في عقد البيع أنه يتبرأ من أَنَّ ضمان العيوب الخفية التي يمكن أن تظهر في الشيء المبيع، فإنه عندئذ لا يكون مسؤولاً تجاه المشتري عما يظهر في المبيع من عيوب، عملاً بالشرط .
ولكن إذا كان البائع عالماً بعيب المبيع وكتمه عن المشتري عند العقد فإن شرط البراءة من ضمان العيب لا يعفيه من هذا الضمان كيلا يتخذ مبدأ احترام الشروط التي يشترطها المتعاقدان ذريعة لأحدهما إلى الغش وسوء النية تحت حماية الشرط.
(۱) طلاق الفرار في اصطلاح المذهب الحنفي (وقد سماه قانون الأحوال الشخصية الجديد لدينا طلاق (التعسف هو أن يطلق الرجل زوجته طلاقاً بائناً دون رضاها في مرض موته، بقصد الفرار من حقها المشروع في الميراث وحرمانها منه. فأوجبوا لها الميراث إذا توفي وهي في العدة سداً لهذا الطريق ولو كان من المحتمل أن الزوج غير قاصد هذا المقصد. (ر : الملحق بهذا الفصل لمزيد من التفصيل).
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. Likewise, the Quran prohibited proposing marriage to a woman in her waiting period after the termination of her marriage by divorce or death of her husband until her waiting period ends, so that her proposal does not lead to a breach of the serious duty of the waiting period required by the family system and previous marital rights. Hence, the marriage contract with a woman in her waiting period, even without consummation, is legally invalid. Among the evidences of the principle of blocking the means in the Prophetic Sunnah is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade building mosques over graves, lest it lead to the worship of great people among the dead. Likewise, the Prophet forbade bequests to an heir, lest it be taken as a means to favor some heirs over others by circumventing the inheritance system, for such favoritism is prohibited legally as we will see in (8/23(1)). Likewise, the Prophet (peace be upon him) forbade the seclusion of a man with an unrelated woman, because this seclusion is a means that can lead to corruption, and it is obligatory to ward off evils. From these examples, the following observations become clear: 1) That the principle of blocking the means was employed by Islamic law in both religious and civil matters. Religious matters like prohibiting building mosques over graves, and civil matters like bequests to an heir. 2) That what is considered in blocking the means is not the bad intention of the doer, but rather the mere fact that the act leads to a result that the law disapproves of, even if the doer has good intention. Hence the Quran forbade insulting the idols of polytheists, even though the one insulting them does so out of faith in Allah and in support of Him. The independent jurists, guided by these texts and similar ones related to the wisdom and policy of legislation which point to the principle of blocking the means, have resorted to this principle in ijtihadi rulings they established on its basis: (1) Among that is what ijtihad has established in more than one school that a divorced wife in a divorce of evasion (talaq al-firar) has the right to inherit from her husband who divorced her, so that his right to divorce is not taken as a means to deprive the wife of her lawful inheritance when he despairs of life with the intent of harm. This falls under preventing abuse of the right, for it is not in the interest to enable people to such abuse. And likewise, the jurists ruled that if the seller stipulates in the sale contract that he disclaims liability for hidden defects that may appear in the sold item, then he is not liable to the buyer for any defects that appear, acting upon the condition. But if the seller knows of the defect and conceals it from the buyer at the time of the contract, then the condition of disclaimer does not exempt him from liability, lest the principle of respecting conditions agreed upon by parties be taken as a means for one of them to cheat and bad faith under the protection of the condition. (1) Talaq al-firar in Hanafi terminology (and the new Personal Status Law has called it 'abusive divorce') is that a man divorces his wife irrevocably without her consent during his terminal illness, intending to evade her lawful inheritance right and deprive her of it. So they made inheritance obligatory for her if he dies while she is in the waiting period, to block this path even if it is possible that the husband did not intend this purpose. (See appendix to this chapter for more detail).
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil) as a subsidiary source of Islamic jurisprudence. The author, Dr. Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, begins by citing Quranic and Prophetic examples to establish the principle. From the Quran, he mentions the prohibition of proposing to a woman in her 'iddah (waiting period) to prevent interference with the obligations of the waiting period, and the invalidity of marriage during 'iddah. From the Sunnah, he cites the prohibition of building mosques over graves to prevent leading to worship of the dead, the prohibition of bequests to an heir to prevent circumventing inheritance law, and the prohibition of seclusion with an unrelated woman to prevent moral corruption. The author then makes two key observations: (1) the principle applies to both religious and civil matters; (2) the principle focuses on the objective outcome of an act, not the subjective intention of the actor. He gives the example of the Quranic prohibition on insulting polytheists' idols, even though the insulter intends good. The author then provides two juristic applications explicitly based on this principle: (a) the Hanafi ruling on 'talaq al-firar' (evasive divorce) where a husband divorces his wife during terminal illness to deprive her of inheritance – the wife is still entitled to inherit despite the divorce, to block this means. (b) A sale contract where the seller disclaims liability for hidden defects; normally the condition is valid, but if the seller knew of the defect and concealed it, the disclaimer is ineffective to prevent the condition from being used for fraud. The footnote explains 'talaq al-firar' in detail as a Hanafi concept.

Key Terms
سد الذرائع (Sadd al-Dhara'i'): A legal principle where an act that is permissible in itself is prohibited to prevent it from leading to a prohibited outcome
طلاق الفرار (Talaq al-Firar): A divorce pronounced by a husband during terminal illness to deprive his wife of inheritance
خطبة (Khitbah): Proposal of marriage
عدة ('Iddah): Waiting period after divorce or death of husband

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following best illustrates the principle of Sadd al-Dhara'i'?
A) Prohibition of building mosques over graves to prevent worship of the dead
B) Permissibility of bequest to an heir because the hadith is abrogated
C) Prohibition of seclusion only if the man has bad intentions
D) Allowing a seller to disclaim liability for known defects as per contract freedom

Key Takeaway
Sadd al-Dhara'i' is a key Hanafi principle that prohibits acts that are otherwise permissible when they typically lead to a prohibited outcome, focusing on the objective result rather than the actor's intention.

Rulings Change with Changing Times: The Maxim and Its Application
Defines a major qa'idah and its rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'la yunkar taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman' to identify which rulings can change and justify the change using the Hanafi framework.

Core Idea
Rulings based on custom and necessity change with time, but fixed divine texts remain unchanged.

This lesson introduces a crucial tool for the mufti: the maxim that ijtihadi rulings can change as circumstances evolve. Relying on the treatise of Ibn Abidin, we explore when and why rulings adapt, ensuring that Sharia remains a living, practical guide.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its key terms
Locate the exact wording of the maxim in the Arabic text: 'لا يُنكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان'. Understand each word: 'taghayyur' (change), 'ahkam' (rulings), 'zaman' (time).
The maxim is a qa'idah wusta, intermediate in scope.
2
Distinguish between changeable and fixed rulings
Recognise that this maxim applies only to ijtihadi rulings (based on custom, necessity, or secondary evidence), not to rulings established by qat'i texts (Quran and mutawatir Sunnah).
Refer to the istithna' in the qawida panel: fixed texts do not change.
3
Examine the causes of change mentioned in the text
Note the two categories: (a) evolution of administrative means and technology (e.g., electricity, cars), and (b) moral decay of the people. These necessitate a re-evaluation of previous rulings to avoid hardship.
Ibn Abidin adds 'occurrence of necessity' as a third cause.
4
Apply the maxim to a modern scenario
Think of a mufti faced with a new contract (e.g., car leasing). Using this maxim, he can adapt classical ijarah rules to the new context, provided the adaptation does not contradict a qat'i text.
The mufti must verify that the change serves maslahah and avoids harm.
5
Note the limitation: rulings based on qat'i dalil do not change
The maxim is restricted by the dabt: 'الأحكام الثابتة بالنص القطعي لا تتغير'. Any ruling that originates from a definitive proof (thubut and dalalah) remains immutable.
This prevents violation of core Sharia principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٨/٥ - تغير الزمان :
من أسباب تبديل الأحكام الاجتهادية في فقه الشريعة الإسلامية اختلاف الأوضاع والأحوال والوسائل الزمنية عما كانت عليه في السابق حينما قررت تلك الأحكام؛ وذلك إما لتطور الأوضاع والأساليب الإدارية والتنظيمية، ولتبدل الوسائل الحيوية كحدوث الكهرباء الآلية والمعامل والسيارات التي غيّرت مجرى الحياة كلها في عصرنا الحاضر وإما لفساد طارىء على أخلاق الناس العامة .
وقد قرر الفقهاء في هذا المقام تلك القاعدة الشهيرة القائلة: «لا يُنكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان» .
وفي هذا الموضوع يقول العلامة ابن عابدين في رسالة النشر العرف إن كثيراً من الأحكام يبنيها المجتهد على ما كان في زمانه، فتختلف باختلاف الزمان لتغير عرف أهله أو لحدوث ضرورة أو لفساد أهل الزمان، بحيث لو بقي الحكم على ما كان عليه للزم منه المشقة والضرر بالناس، ولخالف قواعد الشريعة المبنية على التخفيف والتيسير ودفع الضرر والفساد، لأجل بقاء النظام على أحسن إحكام.
8/5 - Change of Times: Among the reasons for changing ijtihadi rulings in Islamic jurisprudence is the difference of circumstances, conditions, and temporal means from what they were previously when those rulings were established; either due to the development of administrative and organizational conditions and methods, and the change of essential means such as the advent of mechanical electricity, factories and cars that changed the entire course of life in our present age, or due to an emergent corruption in the general morals of people. The jurists have established in this regard the famous rule: 'Change of rulings due to change of times is not be denied.' On this topic, the scholar Ibn Abidin says in his treatise 'Nashr al-'Urf': Many rulings are built by the mujtahid on what was in his time; they vary with the variation of time due to change in the custom of its people, or due to occurrence of necessity, or due to corruption of the people of the time, such that if the ruling remained as it was, it would result in hardship and harm to people, and would contradict the rules of Sharia which are based on alleviation, facilitation, and removal of harm and corruption, for the sake of maintaining the system in the best order.
Source pages p. 108

Commentary
This passage defines the well-known maxim 'لا ينكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان' (change of rulings due to change of times is not denied). It identifies two main causes for changing ijtihadi rulings: (1) evolution of administrative methods and technological means (e.g., electricity, factories, cars), and (2) moral corruption in society. The jurists formulated this rule to ensure that Sharia remains practical and relevant. Ibn Abidin explains that rulings are based on customs, necessities, and the moral state of the time; if a ruling from the past would cause hardship today, it must change to align with the Sharia principles of ease and prevention of harm. This maxim is a manifestation of the wider maxim 'المشقة تجلب التيسير' (hardship brings ease) and 'العادة محكمة' (custom is authoritative). It applies particularly to ijtihadi rulings (not foundational texts) and is used by muftis when fatwas need to adapt to new circumstances.

Key Terms
تغير الزمان (taghayyur al-zaman): اختلاف الأوضاع والأحوال والوسائل الزمنية عن سابقتها
لا يُنكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان (la yunkar taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman): قاعدة فقهية تقرر جواز تغيير الأحكام الاجتهادية تبعاً لتغير الزمان وأحواله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
ما مصدر تغير الأحكام الاجتهادية عند تغير الزمان؟
A) تغير الزمان نفسه
B) تطور الأوضاع والوسائل وفساد الأخلاق
C) رأي الحاكم بلا دليل
D) تغير النصوص الشرعية

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'la yunkar taghayyur al-ahkam bi taghayyur al-zaman' allows muftis to update ijtihadi rulings when customs, means, or morals change, but never at the cost of fixed divine texts.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Authority of Custom: The Maxim 'Custom is Authoritative' and Its Application
Establishes the authority of custom and lists key maxims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-adah muhakkamah' to derive rulings in transactions and identify when custom overrides qiyas via istihsan.

Core Idea
Custom is a binding source in Hanafi fiqh, overriding analogy and acting as a legislative text in the absence of revelation.

This passage from Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi establishes custom (al-urf) as a subsidiary source of Islamic jurisprudence with substantial legal weight. It cites the mawquf hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud as its foundation and lists six key maxims from the Majalla that govern the use of custom. For a Hanafi mufti, understanding these maxims is essential for deriving fatwas in matters of transactions, family law, and other areas where customary practice often determines the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Basis
Find the mawquf athar from Ibn Mas'ud ('What the Muslims consider good...') and understand its evidentiary value in Hanafi usul: it is considered a hujja because a Companion does not legislate based on personal opinion.
This athar is the primary textual basis for the authority of custom.
2
Understand How Custom Overrides Qiyas
Note that custom can override analogy (qiyas) through istihsan when following analogy would cause hardship. This is a distinctive Hanafi method.
Istihsan is often criticized by other schools, but Hanafis rely on it extensively.
3
List and Explain the Six Maxims
From the text, enumerate the six maxims from the Majalla. Focus on the first: 'al-adah muhakkamah' (custom is authoritative). Understand each maxim's application.
The second maxim 'al-haqiqah tutraku bi dalalati al-adah' relates to verbal custom.
4
Apply the Maxim to a Furu Case
Take the furu case from the qawida panel: 'What is recognized by custom is like what is stipulated as a condition.' Apply to a marriage contract where the amount of mahr is unstated but customarily known.
The Hanafi ruling is that the customary mahr is binding.
5
Recognize the Limitation
Custom cannot contradict a clear, imperative text from the Quran or Sunnah. In such cases, text prevails. This is an istithna from the general maxim.
This prevents custom from overriding divine revelation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الباب الثاني: مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
ومعظم العلماء يستدلون على مكانة العرف الفقهية في بناء الأحكام الشرعية بأثر قد قد روي موقوفاً (۱) عن عبد الله بن مسعود، وهو من كبار فقهاء صحابة الرسول عليه الصلاة والسلام أنه قال: «ما رآه المسلمون حَسَناً فهو عند الله حسن».
٤/٦ - سلطان العرف في الفقه الإسلامي إجمالاً.
إنَّ للعرف في الفقه الإسلامي اعتباراً شرعياً في بناء كثير من أنواع الأحكام التي سنرى بيانها مفصَّلاً في بحثنا عن نظرية العرف في الفقه الإسلامي، آخر القسم الثاني من هذا المدخل الفقهي.
والاجتهادات الفقهية في الإسلام متفقة على هذا الاعتبار للعرف وإن كان بينها شيء من التفاوت في حدوده ومداه.
وقد أقام الفقهاء كبير وزن للعرف في ثبوت الحقوق وانتفائها بين الناس في نواح شتى من المعاملات وضروب التصرفات واعتبروا العرف والعادة أصلاً هاماً ومصدراً عظيماً واسعاً تثبت الأحكام الحقوقية بين الناس على مقتضاه في كل ما لا يصادم نصاً تشريعياً خاصاً يمنعه .
فالعُرف في نظرهم دليل شرعي كاف في ثبوت الأحكام الإلزامية والالتزامات التفصيلية بين الناس حيثما لا دليل سواه؛ بل إنه يترك به القياس إذا عارضه لأن القياس المخالف في نتيجته للعرف الجاري يؤدي إلى حرج، فيكون ترك الحكم القياسي والعمل بمقتضى العزف هو من قبيل الاستحسان المقدم على القياس.
أما إذا عارض العرف نصاً تشريعياً آمراً بخلاف الأمر المتعارف ففي اعتبار العرف وعدمه وفي محل هذا الاعتبار ودرجته، تفصيل لا يتسع له هذا المقام وسنبحثه في محله من نظرية العرف كما سنرى هناك أنواع العرف وتقسيمه إلى لفظي وعملي.
٥/٦ - أهم القواعد الفقهية في العرف وسلطانه :
هذا، وقد أثبت الفقهاء قواعد في العرف والعادة كانت أسساً وضوابط لكثير من الأحكام الفرعية القائمة على العرف وذكرت المجلة طائفة منها في المواد/ ٣٦ و ٣٧ و ٣٩ و ٤٠ - ٤٥ .
·

١ - العادة مُحَكَّمة» (١) (المجلة / ٤٠ ) .

(۱) محكمة بتشديد الكاف المفتوحة اسم مفعول من التحكيم، أي أن العرف يجعل حاكماً في إثبات الأحكام الشرعية والالتزامات بين الناس على وفقه، ويلزمهم بها قضاء .
(۲) هذه القاعدة تتعلق بالعرف اللفظي الذي سيأتي بيانه في نظرية العرف. والمراد بالحقيقة هنا المعنى الأصلي للفظ في مقابل المعنى المجازي. أي أن ألفاظ الناس في أقوالهم وتصرفاتهم تحمل على معانيها المتعارفة بينهم، لا على معانيها الحقيقية في أصل اللغة .
Chapter Two: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. Most scholars infer the juristic status of custom in building legal rulings from an athar reported as mawquf from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, one of the great jurists among the Companions of the Messenger (peace be upon him), that he said: 'What the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah.' 4/6 - The authority of custom in Islamic jurisprudence in general. Indeed, custom has a legal consideration in Islamic jurisprudence in building many types of rulings, the details of which we will see in our discussion of the theory of custom, at the end of the second section of this juristic introduction. The juristic ijtihads in Islam agree on this consideration for custom, although there is some variation in its limits and scope. Jurists have given great weight to custom in establishing and negating rights among people in various areas of transactions and types of dispositions, and they considered custom and habit an important foundation and a vast source by which legal rulings are established among people according to it in everything that does not conflict with a specific legislative text prohibiting it. So custom in their view is a sufficient legal proof in establishing binding rulings and detailed obligations among people wherever there is no other proof; rather, analogy is abandoned if it contradicts it, because analogy that contradicts prevailing custom leads to hardship, so abandoning the analogical ruling and acting according to custom is a type of istihsan that takes precedence over analogy. As for when custom contradicts a legislative text commanding contrary to customary matter, then regarding its consideration or not, and the place and degree of this consideration, there is detail that cannot be accommodated here, and we will research it in its place in the theory of custom, as we will see there the types of custom and its division into verbal and practical. 5/6 - The most important juristic maxims regarding custom and its authority: The jurists established maxims regarding custom and habit that were foundations and controls for many subsidiary rulings based on custom. The Majalla mentioned a group of them in articles 36, 37, 39, and 40-45. Among the most important of these juristic maxims related to custom are the following: 1. 'Custom is authoritative' (Majalla art. 40). 2. 'The literal meaning is abandoned by indication of custom' (art. 40). 3. 'The usage of people is a proof that must be acted upon' (art. 37). 4. 'What is recognized by custom is like what is stipulated as a condition' (art. 43). 5. 'Specification by custom is like specification by text' (art. 45). 6. 'It is not denied that rulings change with changing times' (art. 39). Footnotes: (1) Muhakkamah: with shaddah on the open kaf, passive participle from tahkim, meaning that custom is made a judge in establishing legal rulings and obligations among people according to it, and binding them judiciary. (2) This maxim relates to verbal custom, which will be explained in the theory of custom. What is meant by 'literal meaning' (haqiqah) is the original linguistic meaning of a word as opposed to the metaphorical meaning. That is, people's words in their statements and dispositions are interpreted according to their customary meanings, not according to their true meanings in the original language.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is from Al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-Amm by Mustafa Ahmad al-Zarqa, discussing the role of custom ('urf) as a subsidiary source of Islamic jurisprudence. The author begins by citing a famous mawquf athar from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud — 'What the Muslims consider good is good in the sight of Allah' — to establish the foundation for the legal authority of custom. Though the hadith is mawquf (a saying of a Companion, not directly from the Prophet), it holds legislative weight because a Companion cannot say such a thing based on personal opinion; it is considered like a marfu' hadith. The author emphasizes that all jurists agree on the consideration of custom, though they differ on its limits. Custom is a sufficient proof for establishing binding rulings and obligations where no other textual evidence exists. Moreover, it can override qiyas (analogy) when following analogy would lead to hardship; this is considered istihsan (juristic preference). However, if custom contradicts a clear legislative text, then a detailed discussion is needed, which the author postpones. The passage then lists six key legal maxims from the Majalla relating to custom: (1) 'Custom is authoritative' — meaning custom is the judge in establishing rights and obligations. (2) 'The literal meaning is abandoned by indication of custom' — which applies to verbal custom; words are understood according to customary usage, not strict linguistic meanings. (3) 'The usage of people is a proof that must be acted upon.' (4) 'What is recognized by custom is like what is stipulated as a condition.' (5) 'Specification by custom is like specification by text.' (6) 'It is not denied that rulings change with changing times.' These maxims form the backbone of Hanafi fiqh in matters of custom. For a Hanafi mufti, these maxims are essential tools in deriving fatwas, especially in transactions and family law where practice can modify default rulings.

Key Terms
العرف (al-urf): Custom and common practice that is consistent and accepted by people without being opposed to a clear legal text.
الأثر الموقوف (al-athar al-mawquf): A narration from a Companion that is not attributed to the Prophet. It is considered a valid proof in legal matters because the Companion would not legislate on his own.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that abandons a strict analogy in favor of a ruling that better serves justice and ease, often based on custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when custom contradicts a legislative text?
A) Custom is always preferred over the text.
B) The text is always preferred over custom.
C) There is a detailed discussion deferred to later.
D) Both are given equal weight.

Key Takeaway
Custom is a fundamental source in Hanafi fiqh, binding in transactions, and can override analogy through istihsan, but never contradicts clear textual evidence.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Qawaid of 'Urf and Their Furu' Applications
Listing major juristic maxims of custom and their practical applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six major Hanafi qawaid on custom, apply them to furu' cases, and evaluate when custom overrides qiyas but not nass.

Core Idea
Custom is authoritative in Hanafi law, creating obligations like a stipulation, but cannot override an imperative text.

This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm establishes the juristic maxims (qawa'id) that govern the authority of custom ('urf) in Hanafi law. These maxims, codified in the Majalla, serve as foundations for countless subsidiary rulings in mu'amalat. Understanding them is essential for any mufti who must navigate the interplay between custom, qiyas, and textual sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six qawaid
Extract each maxim from the list: al-'ādah muḥakkamah, al-ḥaqīqah tutraku bidalālat al-'ādah, isti'māl al-nās ḥujjah, al-ma'rūf 'urfan ka al-mashrūṭ sharṭan, al-ta'yīn bil-'urf ka al-ta'yīn bil-naṣṣ, lā yunkar taghayyur al-aḥkām bi taghayyur al-azmān.
These are from Majalla articles 36-45.
2
Classify each qawida by rank
Determine which are major (kubra) and which are intermediate (wusta). 'Custom is authoritative' is a kubra; the others are wusta or sughra.
The passage explicitly labels the first as a major maxim.
3
Apply the furuat
For each given case (dower, price, defect, etc.), identify which qawida or combination of qawaid governs the ruling.
Some cases may involve multiple qawaid.
4
Recognize the istithna'at
Note that custom does not apply when it contradicts an imperative legislative text (nass). Also, custom overrides qiyas only when it prevents hardship (istihsan).
This is mentioned in the passage's opening paragraph.
5
Analyze the role of time
Understand that rulings built on custom change when custom changes, as per the last qawida.
This implies a dynamic element in fatwa.

Source Text

الفصل (٦) المصادر التبعية: العرف
القياس إذا عارضه لأن القياس المخالف في نتيجته للعرف الجاري يؤدي إلى حرج، فيكون ترك الحكم القياسي والعمل بمقتضى العرف هو من قبيل الاستحسان المقدم على القياس.
أما إذا عارض العرف نصاً تشريعياً آمراً بخلاف الأمر المتعارف ففي اعتبار العرف وعدمه وفي محل هذا الاعتبار ودرجته، تفصيل لا يتسع له هذا المقام وسنبحثه في محله من نظرية العرف كما سنرى هناك أنواع العرف وتقسيمه إلى لفظي وعملي.
٥/٦ - أهم القواعد الفقهية في العرف وسلطانه :
هذا، وقد أثبت الفقهاء قواعد في العرف والعادة كانت أسساً وضوابط لكثير من الأحكام الفرعية القائمة على العرف وذكرت المجلة طائفة منها
في المواد/ ٣٦ و ٣٧ و ٣٩ و ٤٠ - ٤٥ . و ٢٠ .
·
ومن أهم هذه القواعد الفقهية المتعلقة بالعرف القواعد التالية :
١ - العادة مُحَكَّمة» (١) (المجلة / ٤٠ ) .
٢ - «الحقيقة تترك بدلالة العادة» (۲) (م/ (٤٠) .

ه - التعيين بالعرف كالتعيين بالنص (م/ ٤٥ ) . - لا ينكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الأزمان» (م/٣٩).
(۱) محكمة بتشديد الكاف المفتوحة اسم مفعول من التحكيم، أي أن العرف يجعل حاكماً في إثبات الأحكام الشرعية والالتزامات بين الناس على وفقه، ويلزمهم بها قضاء .
(۲) هذه القاعدة تتعلق بالعرف اللفظي الذي سيأتي بيانه في نظرية العرف. والمراد بالحقيقة هنا المعنى الأصلي للفظ في مقابل المعنى المجازي. أي أن ألفاظ الناس في أقوالهم وتصرفاتهم تحمل على معانيها المتعارفة بينهم، لا على معانيها الحقيقية في أصل اللغة .

الباب الثاني : مصادر الفقه الإسلامي
وسيأتي شرح هذه القواعد، مع بقية القواعد الكلية، في القسم الأخير من هذا المدخل.
وانظر في موضوع هذه القاعدة الأخيرة ما تقدم في بحث الاستصلاح الفصل (٥) وما سيأتي آخر نظرية العرف (ف ١/٧٦ - ٣/٧٨) . وعلى أساس هذه القواعد فرع الفقهاء وقرروا ما لا يحصى من فروع الأحكام في مختلف الأبواب الفقهية والمعاملات:
أ - فتقسيم مهر المرأة مثلاً إلى معجل ومؤجل في الزواج، ومقدار كل منهما إذا لم يبين في عقد النكاح يرجع فيه إلى العرف.
ب - وتقسيم ثمن المبيع وأجرة المأجور إذا لم يصرح به العاقدان وكان فيه عرف جار في بلدة العقد، يلزم فيه الطرفان بحكم العرف.
ج - وما يعد في المبيع عيباً مسوّغاً لفسخ البيع أو لا يعد عيباً إنما يحكم فيه العرف.
-
وتجاوز المستأجر الحدود الجائزة له في استيفاء منفعة المأجور حتى يعتبر متعدياً ضامناً قيمته إذا تلف إنما ميزانه العرف.
وكيفية حفظ الوديعة مما يعد به الوديع مقصراً في حفظها فيضمن إن ضاعت، أو غير مقصر فلا يضمن إنما يعتبر أيضاً فيه العرف
و - واختلاف المعلم مع التلميذ العامل في الصناعات أيهما يستحق على الآخر أجراً يرجع فيه إلى عرف البلدة (المجلة/ ٥٩٦).
ز - وكذا في الإجارة كل ما كان من توابع العمل ولم يشترط على الأجير يعتبر فيه عرف البلدة (المجلة/ ٥٧٤).
إلى غير ذلك من القضايا التي لا تنتهي مما ملئت به فصول الفقه وجعلوا للعرف فيه السلطان المطلق في الحكم.
وغني عن البيان أن ما بني من الأحكام على العرف يتبدل بتبدل العرف . ولذا وضعت القاعدة السالفة الذكر : لا ينكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الزمان
Chapter (6) Subsidiary Sources: Custom. Qiyas when it opposes it, because qiyas whose result contradicts prevailing custom leads to hardship, so leaving the qiyas ruling and acting according to custom falls under istihsan which is given precedence over qiyas. As for when custom opposes an imperative legislative text that contradicts the customary matter, then regarding consideration of custom or not, and the scope and degree of this consideration, there is detail that this place cannot accommodate; we will research it in its proper place in the theory of custom, as we will see there the types of custom and its division into verbal and practical. 5/6 - The most important juristic maxims regarding custom and its authority: The jurists have established maxims regarding custom and habit that were foundations and controls for many subsidiary rulings based on custom. The Majalla mentioned a number of them in Articles 36, 37, 39, and 40-45, and 20. Among these most important juristic maxims related to custom are the following: 1) 'Custom is authoritative' (Majalla 40). 2) 'The literal meaning is abandoned by indication of custom' (M/40). 3) 'People's usage is a proof that must be acted upon' (M/37). 4) 'What is conventionally known is like a stipulated condition' (M/43). 5) 'Specification by custom is like specification by text' (M/45). 6) 'It is not denied that rulings change with changing times' (M/39). (Footnote 1: 'Authoritative' is with shaddah on the open kaaf, the passive participle from 'making authoritative', i.e. custom is made an authority in establishing legal rulings and obligations among people according to it, and the judiciary obliges them to it.) (Footnote 2: This maxim relates to verbal custom, which will be explained in the theory of custom. By 'literal meaning' here is meant the original meaning of the word as opposed to the figurative meaning. That is, the words of people in their statements and transactions are taken to mean their customary meanings among them, not their true linguistic meanings.) The Second Section: Sources of Islamic Jurisprudence. The explanation of these maxims, along with the rest of the universal maxims, will come in the last part of this introduction. And see on the subject of this last maxim what preceded in the discussion of istislah in Chapter (5) and what will come at the end of the theory of custom (vol. 1/76 - 3/78). On the basis of these maxims, the jurists branched out and determined countless subsidiary rulings in various chapters of fiqh and transactions: a) For example, the division of a woman's dower into prompt and deferred in marriage, and the amount of each if not specified in the marriage contract, is referred to custom. b) The division of the price of the sold item and the hire of the hired item if the two contractors did not specify it and there is a prevailing custom in the town of the contract, both parties are bound by the rule of custom. c) What is considered a defect in the sold item justifying rescission of the sale or not a defect is determined by custom. d) The lessee exceeding the permissible limits in utilizing the hired item so that he is considered a transgressor and liable for its value if it perishes, its measure is custom. e) The manner of keeping a trust such that the trustee is considered negligent in its keeping and liable if it is lost, or not negligent and not liable, is also determined by custom. f) Dispute between the teacher and the working apprentice in crafts as to which of them is entitled to payment from the other is referred to the custom of the town (Majalla 596). g) Likewise in hiring, everything that is part of the work and not stipulated upon the hired worker, the custom of the town is considered (Majalla 574). And many other cases that are endless, filling the chapters of fiqh, and they gave custom absolute authority in ruling. It goes without saying that rulings built on custom change with the change of custom. Hence the aforementioned maxim was established: 'It is not denied that rulings change with changing times.'
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from al-Madkhal al-Fiqhi al-'Amm discusses 'urf (custom) as a subsidiary source of Islamic law. The author begins by explaining the relationship between custom and qiyas: when qiyas contradicts prevailing custom, it leads to hardship (haraj), so leaving the analogical ruling and following custom is an instance of istihsan (juristic preference), which takes precedence over qiyas. If custom opposes an explicit textual command, there is a detailed discussion not covered here; it will be treated later in the theory of custom. The passage then lists six major juristic maxims (qawa'id) concerning custom, most of which are codified in the Ottoman Majalla. These maxims are: (1) Custom is authoritative ('ādah muḥakkamah); (2) The literal meaning is abandoned by indication of custom (al-ḥaqīqah tutraku bidalālat al-'ādah); (3) People's usage is a binding proof; (4) What is conventionally known is like a stipulated condition; (5) Specification by custom is like specification by text; (6) It is not denied that rulings change with changing times. The first two maxims are accompanied by explanatory footnotes. The passage then provides numerous furū' (branches or applications) where these maxims are applied: division of dower, price and hire, defects in sale, lessee's liability, trustee's liability, teacher-apprentice disputes, and ancillary work in hiring. Finally, it emphasizes that rulings based on custom change when custom itself changes. This passage demonstrates how the Hanafi school extensively relies on custom in the absence of clear texts, giving it wide authority particularly in transactions (mu'āmalāt).

Key Terms
العادة مُحَكَّمة (al-‘ādah muḥakkamah): Custom is made authoritative in establishing legal rulings and obligations, enforced by the judiciary.
الحقيقة تترك بدلالة العادة (al-ḥaqīqah tutraku bi dalālat al-‘ādah): The literal meaning of a word is abandoned in favor of its customary meaning when people's usage differs from the original linguistic meaning.
المعروف عرفاً كالمشروط شرطاً (al-ma‘rūf ‘urfan ka al-mashrūṭ sharṭan): What is known by custom is like a stipulated condition; obligations arise from custom as if they were explicitly agreed.
لا ينكر تغير الأحكام بتغير الأزمان (lā yunkar taghayyur al-aḥkām bi taghayyur al-azmān): Rulings that are based on custom change when the underlying custom changes; fixed textual rulings remain unchanged, but ijtihadic rulings may adapt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when the price of a sold item is not specified in the contract but a local custom exists?
A) The contract is void due to ambiguity.
B) The contract is valid and the price is determined by the buyer.
C) The contract is valid and both parties are bound by the custom of the town.
D) The contract is valid and the price is based on market value regardless of custom.

Key Takeaway
Custom is a subsidiary source in Hanafi law; it is authoritative in mu'amalat but cannot override explicit legislative texts, and rulings based on custom change with the times.

The Maxim 'Actions are by Intentions'
This passage presents the hadith 'Innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat' with its chain of narrators.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith on intentions and identify its significance as the basis of the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.

Core Idea
Intentions determine the legal value of actions — the Hadith is the root of Hanafi objective-based jurisprudence.

This lesson introduces one of the most foundational hadith in Islamic law, often called the 'half of faith' or 'heart of fiqh.' It is the primary textual basis for the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their objectives), a principle that governs rulings from purification to contracts and even criminal law.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Hadith and Its Chain
Commit the exact Arabic wording of the hadith to memory, along with its primary narrators: Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and Nasa'i, all from 'Umar ibn al-Khattab.
Knowing the chain helps assess the hadith's authority.
2
Understand the Literal Meaning
'Innama' is a restrictive particle, meaning 'only' or 'but.' 'Al-a'mal' means actions/deeds. 'Bi al-niyyat' means 'by intentions.' So the hadith restricts the validity or reward of actions to the accompanying intention.
The word 'innama' is used in Arabic for exclusivity.
3
Connect to the Maxim
The hadith directly gives rise to the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha': every legal act is judged by its underlying objective. Where the external form contradicts the inner intent, the intent prevails.
This maxim is one of the five major (kubra) maxims in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recognize Hanafi Scope Beyond Worship
In Hanafi fiqh, intention is not limited to 'ibadat (worship). It also affects mu'amalat (transactions), jinayat (penalties), and even judicial rulings. For example, a sale may be void if the intent is to disguise a loan with interest.
Some schools restrict the hadith's application to worship only; Hanafis apply it broadly.
5
Identify Its Authority Level
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning and narrated in the Sahihayn, making its transmission (thubut) qat'i. Its meaning is clear but open to interpretation in scope, so its indication (dalala) is considered zanni in some applications.
This combination allows it to be used as a foundational maxim despite being a single hadith.

Source Text

Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This lesson presents the well-known hadith 'Innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat' (Actions are but by intentions). It is one of the most important hadiths in Islamic law, often called the 'heart of fiqh.' The footnote provides its primary sources: Bukhari, Muslim, and others. In Hanafi usul, this hadith is used to validate the consideration of intention in acts of worship (‘ibadat) and transactions (mu‘amalat). For example, a contract may be valid in form but invalid if the intention is to circumvent the law. The hadith is also the basis for the legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their objectives), which is one of the five major legal maxims in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نية (niyya): Intention, the inner resolve to perform an act for Allah's sake.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Al-Bukhari and Muslim only
C) Al-Bukhari, Muslim, Al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and Al-Nasa'i
D) Only 'Umar ibn al-Khattab

Key Takeaway
The hadith 'Innama al-a'mal bi al-niyyat' is the basis for the Hanafi legal maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha,' which requires considering intention in all legal rulings.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Maxim 'Muslims are Bound by Their Conditions'
Presenting the hadith upholding contractual conditions among Muslims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim, identify its hadith source, and apply the Hanafi distinction between valid and void conditions.

Core Idea
Muslims are bound by their stipulations, but only those that do not contradict Shari'a.

This lesson introduces one of the great legal maxims of fiqh: 'al-muslimun 'ala shurotihim.' Derived from a prophetic hadith, this principle upholds the sanctity of contractual agreements in Islamic law. In the Hanafi school, the maxim governs conditions in sales, leases, marriages, and other transactions. However, not every condition is binding — only those that are valid (sahih) according to Shari'a. Understanding this distinction is essential for a mufti when issuing fatwas on contractual disputes.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim in Arabic and English
Commit the exact wording of the maxim to memory: 'المسلمون على شروطهم' — 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' This is the anchor for all later reasoning.
Also transmitted as 'المسلمون عند شروطهم' but the meaning is identical.
2
Identify the hadith source and its authentication
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi, who declared it hasan sahih. Al-Bukhari gave a definitive ta'liq version, lending it additional strength. This is the primary textual evidence (dalil naqli) for the maxim.
Understanding authentication helps assess the hadith's authority in istidlal.
3
Explain the scope: which contracts does this maxim cover?
The maxim is general in Hanafi law, covering all bilateral contracts (sales, leases, marriage, etc.). However, conditions that violate the Quran or Sunna are excluded. This scope is defined by the usul principle that 'amm is subject to takhsis.'
The maxim does not override clear prohibitions.
4
Distinguish valid (sahih) from void (batil) conditions
A valid condition is one that is not prohibited by Shari'a and does not contradict the essence of the contract. A void condition (e.g., requiring something haram or altering the contract's core) is not binding. Hanafi jurists use this distinction to balance contractual freedom with religious boundaries.
Conditions are also categorized as fasid (defective) but the principle is the same.
5
Apply to a case: a stipulation in a sale that the buyer must not resell
In Hanafi fiqh, such a condition is usually considered void because it contradicts the nature of sale (transfer of complete ownership). This shows that the maxim is not absolute; it is limited by other considerations.
This application illustrates the practical thamarah (consequence) of the rule.

Source Text

المسلمون على شروطهم»(۳)

'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (3). (3) Narrated by Abu Dawud in al-Aqdiya (3594) and al-Tirmidhi in al-Ahkam (1352) who said: hasan sahih. Al-Bukhari gave a definitive ta'liq version in al-Ijara (4/451): 'The Prophet said: Muslims are upon their conditions.' This is sahih according to the established principles of hadith sciences. See: Fath al-Bari (17/42).
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This lesson presents the hadith that honors contractual conditions: 'al-muslimun 'ala shurotihim' (Muslims are bound by their stipulations). The footnote notes its authentication. In Hanafi law, this hadith is central to validating contractual terms in sales, leases, marriages, and other transactions. However, conditions that contradict the Quran or Sunna are void. Hanafi jurists use this hadith to balance the principle of 'pacta sunt servanda' with religious boundaries. For example, a stipulation in a sale that something unlawful is permissible would be invalid.

Key Terms
الشرط (al-shart): A condition or stipulation in a contract that both parties agree to.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Muslim
B) Abu Dawud
C) Al-Bukhari
D) Al-Tirmidhi

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-muslimun 'ala shurotihim' binds Muslims to their conditions, but only those that are valid and do not contradict Shari'a.

The Maxim 'Any Condition Not in Allah's Book is Void'
Presenting the hadith voiding conditions contrary to divine law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith that voids conditions contrary to Allah's Book, identify its primary narrators, and apply the maxim to a concrete fiqh scenario.

Core Idea
Conditions contrary to Shari'a are void — the contract survives, the condition is struck down.

This lesson anchors the second major maxim of contractual conditions. The Prophet ﷺ declared that any condition not found in Allah's Book is void. This does not mean all conditions are invalid; rather, conditions that contradict established rulings of the Quran and Sunnah are null. We will explore the hadith text, its narrators, and its application in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the hadith text
Commit the Arabic wording to memory: 'من اشترط شرطاً ليس في كتاب الله تعالى فهو باطل'.
This is a foundational text for contract conditions in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Identify the narrators
Note that it is narrated by al-Bukhari, Muslim, al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud, and al-Nasa'i. This gives it high authenticity.
The hadith is mutafaqun 'alayhi (agreed upon) by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Understand 'Kitab Allah'
Recognize that Hanafis interpret 'Kitab Allah' broadly as the entire Shari'a, including the Quran and established Sunnah.
This prevents an overly literal reading that would exclude Sunnah-based rulings.
4
Apply the maxim to a hypothetical condition
Given a condition that contradicts a clear Shari'a ruling (e.g., waiving maintenance in marriage), derive that the condition is void but the contract remains valid.
The contract itself is not nullified; only the offending condition is struck down.
5
Distinguish from valid conditions
Conditions that are not contrary to Shari'a are binding per the prior maxim 'المسلمون على شروطهم'. This hadith only voids those that conflict.
The two maxims work together: valid conditions are upheld, invalid ones are void.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من اشترط شرطاً ليس في كتاب الله تعالى فهو باطل» (٤) .
(٤) رواه البخاري (٣٢٦/٥) فتح الباري - ط السلفية)، ومسلم (١٥٠٤)، والترمذي (٢١٢٤)، وأبو داود (۳۹۲۹)، والنسائي (٤٦٥٥) وانظر روايات الحديث في جامع الأصول ١٤/٨ - ٩٨.
'Whoever stipulates a condition not in Allah's Book, it is void' (4). (4) Narrated by al-Bukhari (5/326 in Fath al-Bari), Muslim (1504), al-Tirmidhi (2124), Abu Dawud (3929), al-Nasa'i (4655). See also the versions in Jami' al-Usul (14/8-98).
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This lesson presents the hadith that voids any condition not found in the Book of Allah. 'Book of Allah' here means Islamic law as a whole. The footnote provides its primary sources. In Hanafi fiqh, this hadith is complementary to the previous one: conditions are binding unless they contradict the Shari'a. For example, a condition in a marriage contract that the husband will not provide maintenance is void because maintenance is mandated by Allah. Similarly, a condition in a sale that the seller is not liable for defects may be void if it contravenes consumer protection laws derived from Shari'a.

Key Terms
كتاب الله (kitab Allah): The Book of Allah, often interpreted as the Quran or the entire divine law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A condition that the buyer must pay within one week.
B) A condition that the husband will provide a separate residence for his wife.
C) A condition that the wife will not be entitled to any maintenance.
D) A condition that the leased property will be used for storage only.

Key Takeaway
Conditions that contradict the Quran or Sunnah are void; the contract remains valid, but the condition is struck down.

Three Foundational Hadith Principles in Hanafi Jurisprudence
Listing and commentary on three key hadith as constitutional principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify each of the three hadith, state the legal principle derived, and apply the Hanafi interpretation to practical scenarios involving pre-emption, divorce under closure, and burden of proof.

Core Idea
Three weak but foundational hadith shape Hanafi legal rule: prompt pre-emption, invalid divorce under duress, and burden of proof on claimant.

This passage introduces three hadith that, despite weak chains, function as constitutional principles in Hanafi jurisprudence. Pre-emption requires urgency, divorce under closure is void, and the burden of proof rests on the claimant. The author shows how these principles yield wide-ranging applications, from setting limitation periods to determining validity of consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three hadith and their core principles
From the source text, extract each hadith and the legal rule it establishes: (1) pre-emption must be claimed promptly, (2) divorce pronounced in a state of closure is invalid, (3) the burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath on the denier.
Note that the author acknowledges the weak chains but explains that jurists still rely on these hadith for legal reasoning.
2
Analyze the Hanafi interpretation of 'closure'
Focus on the second hadith. Note the different scholarly interpretations: coercion only vs. broader state that impairs free will. The author favors the broader interpretation as 'al-awjah'. Use the madhhab dispute map to understand the opposing views and the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).
The Hanafi position is that any state closing insight or will (anger, coercion, etc.) invalidates divorce.
3
Examine the maxim of burden of proof
The third hadith is a major qawida kulliya. Review the furuat (applications) and istithna' exceptions. Understand how this maxim governs claims and evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
The author likens 'Book of Allah' to divine law as a whole, not just the Quran, similar to modern public order concepts.
4
Apply the principles to practical scenarios
Using the application bridge and practice tasks, think of real-world situations where a mufti would invoke these hadith. For example, setting a time limit for pre-emption claims or evaluating a divorce pronounced in rage.
This step ties the theoretical principles to actual fatwa practice.

والمراد بما ليس في كتاب الله ما يتضمن مخالفة لأسس الشريعة التي قررها القرآن ... فالتعاقد على ذلك واشتراطه باطل كما يعتبر اليوم في النظريات القانونية الحقوقية التعاقد على ما يخالف النظام العام والآداب العامة أو يخالف النصوص القانونية باطلاً. ونظيره قول عمر المتقدم في وصيته القضائية لأبي موسى الأشعري : الصلح جائز إلا صلحاً أحلّ حراماً، أو حرم حلالاً». (ر: ف ٦/٣ الحاشية). فكتاب الله هنا ليس معناه القرآن بل معناه ما كتبه الله وأوجبه، أي شريعته التي شرعها. فالكتاب هنا مصدر بمعنى اسم المفعول أي المكتوب بمعنى المفروض، كما في قوله تعالى في القرآن: إِنَّ الصَّلَوَةَ كَانَتْ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِين كتبا موقوتا ... حق أولوية ممنوح للشريك في العقار يخوله رجحاناً في شراء حصة شريكه
(۱) الشفعة
هي
الآخر إن أراد هذا بيعها لشخص أجنبي. ومعنى الحديث أنّ الأخذ بالشفعة يجب فيه على الشريك الشفيع سرعة الطلب فور علمه بالبيع كسرعة الإنسان في حل عقال البعير بجذب رأس عقدته، وهي في العادة : عقدة انشوطة تحل بجذب طرف الحبل المعقود.
ر: بداية المجتهد لابن رشد ۲/ ۲۲۰ آخر المسألة الثانية من الركن الرابع في الأخذ بالشفعة) . وهذا الحديث لم يبلغ سنده رتبة ،الصحة، فقد رواه ابن ماجه (٢٥٠٠)، والبيهقي ٦ ۱۰۸ من حديث ابن عمر. وقال الحافظ ابن حجر في التلخيص» ٥٦/٣ بعد أن عزاء لابن ماجه والبزار : إسناده ضعيف جداً. وقال ابن حبان: لا أصل له، وقال البيهقي : ليس بثابت»، وقد احتج به الفقهاء على لزوم تحديد مدة قصيرة لطلب الأخذ بالشفعة كيلا يتضرر المشتري من الشريك بطول الانتظار . (۲) اختلف العلماء في تفسير الإغلاق فمنهم من فشره بالإكراه ومنهم من فسره بالغضب الشديد الذي يفقد البصيرة بالعواقب ؛ ومنهم من فسره تفسيراً أعم بكل ما يغلق على الإنسان إرادته وبصيرته من إكراه أو غضب أو نحوهما مما يؤثر في طبيعة التصور أو التبصر أو الاختيار، وهو التفسير الأوجه.
.
والحديث رواه أحمد في مسنده (٢٧٦/٦ ، وأبو داود (۲۱۹۳) في الطلاق، وابن ماجه (٢٠٤٦) والحاكم في المستدرك ۱۹۸/۲ وأبو يعلى والبيهقي (٣٥٧:٧) عن عائشة، واختلفوا في صحته وضعفه (ر) التلخيص الحبير ٢١٠/٣). (۳) رواه البيهقي في السنن ٢٥٢/١٠ عن ابن عباس مرفوعاً بلفظ : اليمين على المدعى عليه . ورواه الترمذي (١٣٤١) عن عبد الله بن عمرو رضي الله عنهما، والدارقطني وإسناده ضعيف كما قال الحافظ ٤/ ۲۰۸ في التلخيص، ولم تبلغ روايته درجة الصحة،
الفصل (۱۰) الدور الأول: عصر النبوة
إلى غير ذلك من أحاديث الأحكام الجليلة الجزيلة .
۳/۱۰ - فالناظر المتأمل في أمثال هذه النصوص التي هي دساتير في أفكارها مواقير (۱) في أثمارها، يستطيع أن يتبين مدى ما يمكن أن تعطيه في التطبيقات الجزئية والتفريعات الفقهية العملية من أحكام وأفهام مختلفة، ضمن حدود النظر الصحيح المعقول.
فحديث: «الشفعة كحل العقال مثلاً يصلح أساساً لفكرة التقادم (مرور الزمن وتحديد المدة للمطالبة ببعض الحقوق ولاستعمال بعض الخيارات العقدية كخيار الرؤية ،والعيب ولمراجعة بعض الدرجات القضائية للاعتراض على الأحكام البدائية عندما تؤسس المحاكم على درجات كما في زماننا اليوم مما تقضي المصلحة تحديد مدة له تحت طائلة سقوط حق المطالبة القضائية عند إهمالها في المدة المحددة.
Chapter Three: Stages of Development of Islamic Fiqh and Its Characteristics. = 'Pre-emption is like undoing the halter' (1). 'No divorce in closure' (2). 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies' (3). And what is meant by 'not in the Book of Allah' is anything that implies contravention of the foundations of Shariah established by the Quran... so contracting on that and stipulating it is invalid, just as today in legal rights theories, contracting on what violates public order and public morals or violates legal texts is invalid. Its analogue is the saying of Umar in his judicial will to Abu Musa al-Ash'ari: 'Reconciliation is permitted except a reconciliation that makes lawful something forbidden or makes forbidden something lawful.' (See: F 6/3 footnote). So 'Book of Allah' here does not mean the Quran but rather what Allah has prescribed and obligated, i.e., His Shariah which He legislated. So 'book' here is a verbal noun in the sense of the passive participle, meaning 'what is written' in the sense of 'what is ordained', as in His statement in the Quran: 'Indeed, prayer has been upon the believers a prescribed timed obligation' ... Pre-emption is a right of priority granted to a partner in real property, entitling him to preference in purchasing his partner's share if the latter wants to sell it to a stranger. The meaning of the hadith is that taking by pre-emption requires the partner-pre-emptor to claim promptly as soon as he knows of the sale, like the speed of a person in untying the halter of a camel by pulling the head of its knot, which is usually a slip knot that is undone by pulling the end of the tied rope. (Ref: Bidayat al-Mujtahid by Ibn Rushd 2/220, end of the second issue of the fourth pillar on taking by pre-emption). This hadith's chain has not reached the rank of soundness; Ibn Majah (2500) and al-Bayhaqi (6/108) narrated it from Ibn Umar. Al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in al-Talkhis (3/56) after attributing it to Ibn Majah and al-Bazzar: 'Its chain is very weak.' Ibn Hibban said: 'It has no basis,' and al-Bayhaqi said: 'It is not established.' Yet jurists have used it as evidence for the necessity of setting a short period for claiming pre-emption to avoid harm to the buyer from the partner's delay. (2) Scholars differed in interpreting 'closure'; some interpreted it as coercion, some as intense anger that blinds one to consequences, and some interpreted it more broadly as anything that closes one's will and insight, such as coercion, anger, or the like, affecting the nature of perception, insight, or choice, and this is the most appropriate interpretation. The hadith was narrated by Ahmad in his Musnad (6/276), Abu Dawud (2193) in the book of divorce, Ibn Majah (2046), al-Hakim in al-Mustadrak (2/198), Abu Ya'la, and al-Bayhaqi (7/357) from Aisha, and they differed on its authenticity and weakness (see: al-Talkhis al-Habir 3/210). (3) Narrated by al-Bayhaqi in al-Sunan (10/252) from Ibn Abbas as marfu' with the wording: 'The oath is on the defendant.' Also narrated by al-Tirmidhi (1341) from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As, and al-Daraqutni, and its chain is weak as al-Hafiz said in al-Talkhis (4/208), and its narration did not reach the level of soundness. Chapter (10) The First Era: The Age of Prophethood. In addition to other noble hadith of rulings, abundant. 3/10 - The contemplative observer of such texts, which are constitutions in their ideas, heavy-laden with fruit in their outcomes, can discern the extent of what they can yield in specific applications and practical juristic subdivisions of different rulings and understandings, within the limits of sound rational consideration. For example, the hadith 'Pre-emption is like undoing the halter' is suitable as a basis for the idea of prescription (passage of time and setting a period for claiming some rights and for using certain contractual options like option of inspection and defect, and for reviewing some judicial degrees to challenge primary judgments when courts are established on degrees as in our time today, where public interest requires setting a period for it under penalty of losing the right of judicial claim if neglected within the specified period.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage presents three key hadith that serve as foundational constitutional principles (دساتير) in Islamic jurisprudence. The author lists them and then offers commentary. First, the hadith on pre-emption (الشفعة) likens the prompt claim required of the pre-emptor to the quick release of a camel's halter. Although the author notes the chain is weak, fuqaha have used it to establish a limitation period for claiming pre-emption to protect the buyer from indefinite waiting. Second, the hadith 'No divorce in closure' (لا طلاق في إغلاق) is interpreted variously as coercion, extreme anger, or anything that clouds one's free will and insight. The author favors the broader interpretation, which aligns with Hanafi concern for valid consent. Third, the hadith 'The burden of proof is on the claimant and the oath is on the one who denies' (البينة على المدعي واليمين على من أنكر) is a fundamental rule of evidence, despite its weak chain. The author then explains that the phrase 'not in the Book of Allah' in the earlier statement refers not to the Quran literally but to Allah's prescribed law (ما كتبه الله وأوجبه). He draws an analogy to modern legal concepts of public order and public morals. After listing these hadith, the author emphasizes that they are 'constitutions in their ideas' (دساتير في أفكارها), capable of yielding many practical applications. He demonstrates this by showing how the pre-emption hadith can serve as the basis for the legal concept of prescription (التقادم), limitation periods for contractual options (like option of inspection), and appellate deadlines in multi-tiered court systems. This illustrates the Hanafi methodology of deriving broad legal principles from specific hadith, even when the chain is not strictly authentic, using them as tools for juristic reasoning (جعالة). The passage underscores the role of these hadith as foundational 'dabt' (sub-maxims) that guide detailed rulings.

Key Terms
الشفعة (al-shuf‘ah): A right of priority granted to a partner in real property to buy his partner's share should the partner wish to sell it to a third party.
الإغلاق (al-ighlaq): Closure: a state that closes one's will and insight, such as coercion, extreme anger, or the like.
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence; proof that a claimant must produce to support his claim, typically through witnesses or documents.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It establishes the right of pre-emption without any time limit.

Key Takeaway
Despite weak chains, these three hadith function as foundational principles in Hanafi jurisprudence, guiding rulings on pre-emption, validity of divorce under duress, and burden of proof.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
Intent Determines Ownership: Al-Umur bi-Maqasidiha in Ikhraz
Legal maxim application with furuat examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine ownership of acquired mubahat and identify the requirement of intention in ihraz.

Core Idea
Ownership of unowned things depends on the intention behind the act of acquisition, not just physical possession.

This lesson explores the first cause of ownership: acquisition of permissible things (ikhraz al-mubahat). The Hanafi school distinguishes between mere physical control and intentional acquisition. The key is the legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'—matters are judged by intentions. We will see how a simple act like setting a net or building a tower can or cannot create ownership based on the actor's purpose.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its rank
Identify the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and note that it is one of the five major legal maxims (qawida kubra) governing all of fiqh.
This maxim is recorded as Article 2 in the Majalla.
2
Analyze the net example
Consider the two scenarios for a hunter's net: one for hunting, one for drying. Determine who is the acquirer (muhriz) by linking the act to the intention.
The physical act is the same; only the intention differs.
3
Extend to vessel and tower examples
Apply the same analysis to placing a rainwater vessel and building a pigeon tower. Identify the condition that triggers ownership.
Ability to take without hunting is also relevant.
4
Generalize the principle
Formulate the rule: For mubahat, ownership requires both physical taking (qabd) and the intention to acquire (niyyat al-tamalluk). The maxim filters which acts count as acquisition.
Contrast with other schools if needed, but stay Hanafi.
5
Note the exception for war spoils
Understand that war spoils are treated as mubahat because enemy property lacks protected ownership. However, the intention of the state in waging war is distinct.
This is a sub-application of the maxim in international law.

Source Text
