الفصل (۷۸) تغير الأحكام الاجتهادية لتطور الوسائل
فبناءً على ذلك يصبح من الضروري في فقه الشريعة أن يعتبر التسجيل العقد العقاري حكم التسليم الفعلي للعقار في ظل هذه الأوضاع القانونية التنظيمية الجديدة تعتدها، وهي (1).
٣ - أوجب الشرع الإسلامي على كل زوجة تُطَلَّق من زوجها عدة أن تمكث مدة معينة يمنع فيها زواجها برجل آخر. وذلك لمقاصد شرعية تعتبر من النظام العام في الإسلام أهمها تحقق فراغ رحمها من الحمل منعاً لاختلاط الأنساب.
وكان في الحالات التي يقضي فيها القاضي بالتطليق الجبري أو بفسخ النكاح تعتبر المرأة داخلة في العدة ويبدأ حساب عدتها من فور قضاء القاضي بالفرقة، لأن حكم القاضي في الماضي كان يصدر مبرماً واجب التنفيذ فوراً، لأنَّ القضاء مؤسس شرعاً على درجة واحدة، وليس فوق أحد له حق النظر في قضائه.
القاضي
لكن اليوم قد أصبح النظام القضائي لدينا يجعل قضاء القاضي خاضعاً للطعن بطريق الاستئناف أو بطريق النقض أو بكليهما. وهذا التنظيم القضائي الجديد لا ينافي الشرع لأنه من الأمور الاستصلاحية الخاضعة لقاعدة المصالح المرسلة (ر: ف ٧/٥ وما بعدها).
فإذا قضى القاضي اليوم بالفرقة بين الزوجين وجب أن لا تدخل المرأة في العدة إلا بعد أن يصبح قضاؤه مبرماً غير خاضع لطريق من طرق الطعن القضائي، وذلك إما بانقضاء المهل القانونية دون طعن من الخصم، أو بإبرام الحكم المطعون فيه لدى المحكمة المطعون لديها ورفضها للطعن حين ترى الحكم موافقاً للأصول. فمن هذا الوقت يجب اليوم أن تدخل المرأة في العدة ويبدأ حسابها، لا من وقت صدور الحكم الابتدائي، لأنها لو اعتدت منذ صدور الحكم الابتدائي لربما تنقضي عدتها وتتحرر من آثار الزوجية قبل الفصل في الطعن المرفوع على حكم القاضي الأول بانحلال الزوجية، ثم ينقض هذا الحكم لخلل تراه المحكمة العليا فيه. وهذا النقض يرفع الحكم السابق ويوجب عودة الزوجية.
فكيف يمكن ذلك بعد أن تصبح المرأة متحررة من آثار الزواج بانقضاء عدتها وقد ساغ لها أن تتزوج زوجاً آخر، وقد تكون تزوّجت فعلاً؟! .
لذلك يجب أن يعتبر الحكم الابتدائي الأول بالفرقة كحكم معلق على الإبرام أي يعتبر مشروع (فرقة لا تسري نتائجه، وخاصة منها العدة إلا من بعد صيرورته مبرماً.
وقبل ذلك تبقى الزوجية قائمة بكل نتائجها رغم قضاء القاضي بالفرقة نظراً لتبدل الأوضاع القضائية عما كانت عليه في الماضي عندما كان قضاء القاضي الشرعي يصدر على درجة واحدة مبرماً لا معقب عليه.
ولا محذور في اعتبار الزوجية قائمة قبل انبرام الحكم بالفرقة، بل إنَّ لذلك نظيراً في الشرع يشبهه من هذا الوجه وهو الطلاق الرجعي الذي يوقعه الزوج نفسه. فإن الزوجية تبقى مع الطلاق الرجعي قائمة من كل وجه بين الزوجين رغم الطلاق ما دامت المرأة في العدة، حتى إن المتعة الزوجية تظل حلالاً بينهما وتقع بها الرجعة، وكذا لو مات أحدهما خلال العدة يرثه الآخر. فالطلاق الرجعي في النظام الإسلامي هو كما يقال بلغة العصر: مشروع فرقة قابل للرفع والإلغاء بالمراجعة. فإذا انقضت عدة المرأة دون رجعة من الزوج المطلق فعندئذ تقع البينونة (الفرقة).
فيجب أن يعتبر نظير ذلك بالنسبة إلى بدء عدة المرأة في حالة التطليق
Chapter (78): Change of Ijtihadic Rulings Due to the Evolution of Means. Consequently, it becomes necessary in the fiqh of Sharia to consider the registration of a real estate contract as equivalent to actual delivery of the property under these new regulatory legal circumstances that [the law] adopts, and it is (1). 3 - Islamic law obligated every wife who is divorced by her husband to observe a waiting period ('iddah) for a specific duration during which her marriage to another man is prohibited. This is for legitimate purposes considered part of public order in Islam, the most important of which is verifying the emptiness of her womb from pregnancy to prevent mixing of lineages. In cases where the judge rules for compulsory divorce or annulment of marriage, the woman used to be considered as entering the 'iddah and her 'iddah calculation would begin immediately upon the judge's ruling of separation, because the judge's ruling in the past used to be issued as final and immediately enforceable, since the judiciary was established legally on one level, and there was no one above to have the right to review his ruling. But today the judicial system in our country has made the judge's ruling subject to challenge by way of appeal or cassation or both. This new judicial organization does not contradict the Sharia because it is among matters of istislah (public interest) subject to the principle of masalih mursala (unrestricted interests) (see 7/5 ff.). So if the judge today rules for separation between the spouses, the woman should not enter the 'iddah except after his ruling becomes final, no longer subject to any means of judicial challenge. That is either by the expiry of legal deadlines without challenge from the opponent, or by the ratification of the challenged ruling by the appellate court and its rejection of the challenge when it sees the ruling as conforming to principles. From this time onwards, the woman must enter the 'iddah and its calculation begins, not from the time of the initial ruling. Because if she observed 'iddah from the initial ruling, perhaps her 'iddah would end and she would be free from the effects of marriage before the decision on the appeal raised against the first judge's ruling of dissolution of marriage, then this ruling is overturned due to a defect seen by the higher court. This overturning nullifies the previous ruling and necessitates the return of the marriage. How can that be after the woman has become free from the effects of marriage due to the expiry of her 'iddah, and she has been allowed to marry another husband, and might have actually married?! Therefore, the first initial ruling of separation must be considered as a suspended ruling pending finalization, i.e., it is considered a (separation that does not take effect, especially the 'iddah, except after it becomes final). Before that, the marriage remains in effect with all its consequences despite the judge's ruling of separation, due to the change in judicial circumstances from what they were in the past when the ruling of the Sharia judge used to be issued on one level, final and not subject to appeal. There is no harm in considering the marriage as existing before the finalization of the separation ruling. Indeed, there is a parallel in Sharia similar to it in this respect: revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) pronounced by the husband himself. For the marriage remains in every respect between the spouses despite the divorce as long as the woman is in 'iddah, to the extent that conjugal relations remain permissible between them and revocation (ruju') takes place, and similarly if one of them dies during the 'iddah, the other inherits from him. Revocable divorce in the Islamic system is, as it is said in modern language: a project of separation that is subject to lifting and cancellation by revocation. So when the woman's 'iddah expires without the divorcing husband revoking, then the final separation (baynuna) occurs. So the parallel must be considered regarding the beginning of the woman's 'iddah in the case of judicial divorce.
Source pages p. 893

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the principle that ijtihadic rulings can change when the underlying means or circumstances evolve (taghayyur al-ahkam al-ijtihadiyya li-tatawwur al-wasa'il). The author, Mustafa al-Zarqa, provides two applications: first, the registration of a real estate contract is now considered equivalent to actual delivery because of modern legal systems; second, and more detailed, the start of 'iddah in judicial divorce is affected by the availability of appeal. Historically, a judge's ruling was final and immediately enforceable, so the 'iddah began at once. Today, rulings can be appealed or challenged via cassation. Since this appeals system is based on public interest (masalih mursala) and is not contrary to Sharia, the 'iddah should only start when the ruling becomes final (mubram) and no longer subject to appeal. Waiting until the initial ruling would risk absurd consequences: if the 'iddah ends and the woman remarries, then the appellate court overturns the divorce, the original marriage revives, but she is already in a new marriage. Therefore, the initial ruling is considered suspended (ta'liq) pending finalization, analogous to revocable divorce (talaq raj'i) where the marriage continues during 'iddah. This shows the Hanafi concept of 'urf (custom) and changing circumstances influencing fatwa. The passage emphasizes that a mufti must consider modern legal systems when determining the application of Sharia rules.

Key Terms
العدة (al-'iddah): The waiting period observed by a woman after separation from her husband before she can remarry, primarily to ensure no pregnancy exists.
الحكم الابتدائي (al-hukm al-ibtida'i): The initial ruling issued by a court of first instance, which is subject to appeal.
الإبرام (al-ibram): The finalization of a ruling, making it no longer subject to judicial challenge.
الطلاق الرجعي (al-talaq al-raj'i): Revocable divorce where the husband has the right to take back his wife during the 'iddah period without a new marriage contract.
المصالح المرسلة (al-masalih al-mursala): Unrestricted public interests not explicitly regulated by Sharia texts but consistent with its principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under a modern judicial system with appeal possibilities, when does the 'iddah begin for a woman divorced by a court ruling?
A) Immediately upon the initial court ruling.
B) Only after the ruling becomes final and no longer subject to appeal.
C) After the woman receives the written judgment.
D) At the end of the appeal period regardless of whether an appeal is filed.

Key Takeaway
The start of 'iddah in judicial divorce shifts from the initial ruling to its finalization because the modern appeal system destroys the classical condition of finality, illustrating the qawida that ijtihadic rulings change with evolving means.
